<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Hollywood Airport" redirects here. For the airport serving Hollywood, Los Angeles, see <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Burbank_Airport" title="Hollywood Burbank Airport">Hollywood Burbank Airport</a>.</div>

<p><b>Fort Lauderdale–Hollywood International Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>FLL</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>KFLL</b>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">FAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Location_identifier" title="Location identifier">LID</a>: <b>FLL</b>) is a major public airport in <a href="/wiki/Broward_County,_Florida" title="Broward County, Florida">Broward County, Florida</a>, United States, and is one of three airports serving the <a href="/wiki/Miami_metropolitan_area" title="Miami metropolitan area">Miami metropolitan area</a>. The airport is off <a href="/wiki/Interstate_595_in_Florida" class="mw-redirect" title="Interstate 595 in Florida">Interstate 595</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_1_in_Florida" title="U.S. Route 1 in Florida">U.S. Route 1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Road_A1A" title="Florida State Road A1A">Florida State Road A1A</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Road_5" title="Florida State Road 5">Florida State Road 5</a> bounded by the cities <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lauderdale,_Florida" title="Fort Lauderdale, Florida">Fort Lauderdale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hollywood,_Florida" title="Hollywood, Florida">Hollywood</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dania_Beach,_Florida" title="Dania Beach, Florida">Dania Beach</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> 3 miles (5&#160;km) southwest of downtown Fort Lauderdale<sup id="cite_ref-FAA_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAA-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> and 21 miles (34&#160;km) north of Miami. The airport is near cruise line terminals at <a href="/wiki/Port_Everglades" title="Port Everglades">Port Everglades</a> and is popular among tourists bound for the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>. With over 700 daily flights to 135 domestic and international destinations, FLL has become an intercontinental gateway since the late 1990s, although <a href="/wiki/Miami_International_Airport" title="Miami International Airport">Miami International Airport</a> still handles most long-haul flights. FLL serves as a primary airport for the Miami, Fort Lauderdale, Pompano Beach, Boca Raton areas.
</p><p>It is the largest base for <a href="/wiki/Spirit_Airlines" title="Spirit Airlines">Spirit Airlines</a>, catering mainly to the airline's international to domestic network, and it is a focus city for <a href="/wiki/Allegiant_Air" title="Allegiant Air">Allegiant Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">JetBlue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Air_Shuttle" title="Norwegian Air Shuttle">Norwegian Air Shuttle</a>. In November 2019, the top five air carriers by market share were <a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">JetBlue</a> at 23.8%, <a href="/wiki/Spirit_Airlines" title="Spirit Airlines">Spirit Airlines</a> at 22.8%, <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Airlines" title="Southwest Airlines">Southwest Airlines</a> at 19.6% <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a> at 10.1%, and <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a> at 6.0%.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> FLL is ranked as the 18th busiest airport (in terms of passenger traffic) in the United States, as well as the nation's 14th busiest international air gateway and one of the world's 50 busiest airports. FLL is classified by the <a href="/wiki/US_Federal_Aviation_Administration" class="mw-redirect" title="US Federal Aviation Administration">US Federal Aviation Administration</a> as a "major hub" facility serving commercial air traffic. In 2019, the airport processed 36,747,622 passengers<sup id="cite_ref-ACI_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACI-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> (2.2% more than 2018) including 8,844,072 international passengers (2.7% more than 2018).
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Fort_Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood_International_Airport&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Fort+Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood+International+Airport%22">"Fort Lauderdale–Hollywood International Airport"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Fort+Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood+International+Airport%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Fort+Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood+International+Airport%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Fort+Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood+International+Airport%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Fort+Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood+International+Airport%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Fort+Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood+International+Airport%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">February 2017</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Merle Fogg Airport opened on an abandoned 9-hole <a href="/wiki/Golf_course" title="Golf course">golf course</a> on May 1, 1929. At the start of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, it was commissioned by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> and renamed <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_Fort_Lauderdale" title="Naval Air Station Fort Lauderdale">Naval Air Station Fort Lauderdale</a>. The base was initially used for refitting civil airliners for military service before they were ferried across the Atlantic to Europe and North Africa. NAS Fort Lauderdale later became a main training base for <a href="/wiki/Naval_Aviator" class="mw-redirect" title="Naval Aviator">Naval Aviators</a> and enlisted naval air crewmen flying the <a href="/wiki/Grumman_TBF_Avenger" title="Grumman TBF Avenger">Grumman TBF and TBM Avenger</a> for the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Navy">U.S. Navy</a> and <a href="/wiki/U.S._Marine_Corps" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Marine Corps">U.S. Marine Corps</a> aboard aircraft carriers and from expeditionary airfields ashore. NAS Fort Lauderdale was the home base for <a href="/wiki/Flight_19" title="Flight 19">Flight 19</a>, the five TBM Avengers that disappeared in December 1945, leading in part to the notoriety of the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Triangle" title="Bermuda Triangle">Bermuda Triangle</a>.
</p><p>NAS Fort Lauderdale closed on October 1, 1946 and was transferred to county control, becoming <b>Broward County International Airport</b>.
</p><p>Commercial flights to <a href="/wiki/Nassau,_Bahamas" title="Nassau, Bahamas">Nassau</a> began on June 2, 1953, and domestic flights began in 1958–1959: <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Airlines" title="Northeast Airlines">Northeast Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Airlines_(NA)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Airlines (NA)">National Airlines</a> DC-6Bs flew nonstop to <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">Idlewild</a>, and Northeast flew nonstop to Washington National. In 1959 the airport opened its first permanent terminal building and assumed its current name.
</p><p>In 1966, the airport averaged 48 airline operations a day; in 1972, it averaged 173 a day.
</p><p>The Feb 1966 Official Airline Guide shows three nonstop departures to <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">New York–Kennedy</a> and no other nonstop flights beyond Tampa and Orlando. Five years later. FLL had added nonstop flights to <a href="/wiki/Hartsfield%E2%80%93Jackson_Atlanta_International_Airport" title="Hartsfield–Jackson Atlanta International Airport">Atlanta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baltimore%E2%80%93Washington_International_Airport" title="Baltimore–Washington International Airport">Baltimore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Logan_International_Airport" title="Logan International Airport">Boston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Niagara_International_Airport" title="Buffalo Niagara International Airport">Buffalo</a>, <a href="/wiki/O%27Hare_International_Airport" title="O&#39;Hare International Airport">Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Hopkins_International_Airport" title="Cleveland Hopkins International Airport">Cleveland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Metropolitan_Airport" title="Detroit Metropolitan Airport">Detroit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis%E2%80%93Saint_Paul_International_Airport" title="Minneapolis–Saint Paul International Airport">Minneapolis</a>, <a href="/wiki/LaGuardia_Airport" title="LaGuardia Airport">New York–La Guardia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">Newark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_International_Airport" title="Philadelphia International Airport">Philadelphia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_International_Airport" title="Pittsburgh International Airport">Pittsburgh</a>. (Northeast's nonstop to <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">Los Angeles</a> had already been dropped.)
</p><p>By 1974, the airport was served by <a href="/wiki/Braniff_International_Airways" title="Braniff International Airways">Braniff International Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Air_Lines" title="Eastern Air Lines">Eastern Air Lines</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Airlines_(NA)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Airlines (NA)">National Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Orient_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Northwest Orient Airlines">Northwest Orient Airlines</a>, Shawnee Airlines and <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a>. Delta and Eastern were the dominant carriers, with 12 and 14 routes from FLL respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> By 1979, following deregulation, <a href="/wiki/Air_Florida" title="Air Florida">Air Florida</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahamasair" title="Bahamasair">Bahamasair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida_Airlines" title="Florida Airlines">Florida Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mackey_International_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Mackey International Airlines">Mackey International Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic Airlines">Republic Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trans_World_Airlines" title="Trans World Airlines">Trans World Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Airlines" title="Western Airlines">Western Airlines</a> also served the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Low-cost airline traffic grew in the 1990s, with <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Airlines" title="Southwest Airlines">Southwest</a> opening its base in 1996, <a href="/wiki/Spirit_Airlines" title="Spirit Airlines">Spirit</a> in 1999, and <a href="/wiki/JetBlue_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="JetBlue Airways">JetBlue</a> in 2000. <a href="/wiki/Spirit_Airlines" title="Spirit Airlines">Spirit Airlines</a> made FLL a <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">hub</a> in 2002. In 2003, <a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">JetBlue</a> made FLL a <a href="/wiki/Focus_city" class="mw-redirect" title="Focus city">focus city</a>. <a href="/wiki/US_Airways" title="US Airways">US Airways</a> also planned a hub at Fort Lauderdale in the mid-2000s as part of its reorganization strategy before its merger with <a href="/wiki/America_West" class="mw-redirect" title="America West">America West</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Low-cost competition forced several major legacy airlines to cut back service to FLL, with United pulling out of the airport entirely in 2008<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> moving its New York and Los Angeles services to <a href="/wiki/West_Palm_Beach_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="West Palm Beach International Airport">West Palm Beach</a> in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">2005 hurricane season</a> FLL was affected by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">Hurricane Wilma</a>. Katrina struck land in late August as a <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" class="mw-redirect" title="Saffir–Simpson Hurricane Scale">Category 1</a> and made landfall on Keating Beach just two miles from the airport (near the border of <a href="/wiki/Broward_County,_Florida" title="Broward County, Florida">Broward</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miami%E2%80%93Dade_County,_Florida" class="mw-redirect" title="Miami–Dade County, Florida">Miami–Dade</a> counties) with 80&#160;mph (130&#160;km/h) winds but caused only minor damage; however, the airport was closed for about a 48-hour period. However, when Hurricane Wilma made landfall in October roof damage was reported along with broken windows, damaged jetways, and destroyed canopies. The airport was closed for a period of 5 days. Hurricane Wilma was a <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" class="mw-redirect" title="Saffir–Simpson Hurricane Scale">Category 2</a> when its center passed to the west of FLL.
</p><p>In February 2007, the airport started fees to all users, including private aircraft. FLL is one of the few airports to administer fees to private pilots. A minimum charge of $10 is assessed on landing private aircraft.
</p><p>On October 11, 2016, <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a> announced that they would operate a flight from <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a> to Ft. Lauderdale daily using a Boeing 777-200LR. The airline decided on Fort Lauderdale instead of <a href="/wiki/Miami_International_Airport" title="Miami International Airport">Miami</a>, which has considerably longer runways and better facilities for long haul flights, because of its codeshare agreement with <a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">JetBlue</a>. The airline started flying in December 2016. On October 27, 2016, <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> announced a flight from <a href="/wiki/London_Gatwick" class="mw-redirect" title="London Gatwick">London Gatwick</a> to Ft. Lauderdale three times a week, which began on July 6, 2017.
</p><p>In 2018, <a href="/wiki/NORAD" class="mw-redirect" title="NORAD">NORAD</a> announced that it would be stationing fighter jets at the airport during President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump's</a> trips to <a href="/wiki/Mar-a-Lago" title="Mar-a-Lago">Mar-a-Lago</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities">Facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Fort Lauderdale–Hollywood International Airport covers 1,380 acres (558&#160;ha) and has two <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">runways</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-FAA_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAA-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>10L/28R: 9,000 x 150&#160;ft (2,743 x 46 m) Asphalt</li>
<li>10R/28L: 8,000 x 150&#160;ft (2,438 x 46 m) Concrete (Opened September 18, 2014.)<sup id="cite_ref-runway_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-runway-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>In March 2019, there were 109 aircraft based at this airport: 8 single-engine, 21 multi-engine, 64 jet and 16 helicopter.<sup id="cite_ref-FAA_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAA-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Silver_Airways" title="Silver Airways">Silver Airways</a> has its headquarters in Suite 201 of the 1100 Lee Wagener Blvd building.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/Chalk%27s_International_Airlines" title="Chalk&#39;s International Airlines">Chalk's International Airlines</a> existed, its headquarters was on the grounds of the airport in an unincorporated area.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction">Construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl><dt>Expansion of runway 10R/28L</dt></dl>
<p>In 2003, plans to expand the facility started. Proposed improvements included an extension of runway 10R/28L,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> construction and modifications to the airport's taxiway system to provide for increased speed, improved inter-terminal passenger movement, and extensive terminal upgrades. The plan was updated a second time on April 25, 2006. Complaints by nearby communities about noise, along with concerns about buyout requirements, delayed construction that is expected to keep the airport viable through 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 5, 2007, <a href="/wiki/Broward_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Broward County">Broward County</a> commissioners voted six to three in favor of extending the southern 10R/28L runway. The proposal looked to extend the runway to 8,000 feet (2,400&#160;m) in order to accommodate larger aircraft and to allow airplanes to land side by side at the same time. The proposal was approved by the FAA and expansion of the south runway was completed in September 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-runway_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-runway-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The crosswind runway (13/31) was decommissioned on May 6, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Adrain_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adrain-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> All four terminals now have 63 gates total; that number will increase to 97 with the completion of a new long-haul international Terminal Four and Concourse A at Terminal One. By 2020, Ft. Lauderdale–Hollywood is projected to handle 36 million passengers annually.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Demolition and reconstruction of Terminal Four</dt></dl>
<p>During and after the expansion of runway 10R/28L, reconstruction of Terminal Four will begin at the cost of $450 million. The H concourse will be demolished to build the new "G" concourse. In this process four new gates will be added. Concession space will be increased from 2,128 square feet (197.7&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) to 28,000 square feet (2,600&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) and a secure walkway will be added to connect terminals three and four.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>North runway maintenance</dt></dl>
<p>On June 2019, the north runway closed for maintenance, reducing the number of passengers flying in until October 2019. The airport had last seen major renovations on the north runway since 2004, with parts of the runway still dating back to 1943.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminals">Terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Fort Lauderdale–Hollywood International Airport has four terminals. Terminal 1, commonly referred to as "The New Terminal," opened in stages between 2001 and 2003 and was designed by <a href="/wiki/Hellmuth,_Obata_and_Kassabaum" class="mw-redirect" title="Hellmuth, Obata and Kassabaum">Hellmuth, Obata and Kassabaum</a><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> and Cartaya Associates.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The other three terminals were constructed in 1986 and designed by <a href="/wiki/Reynolds,_Smith_%26_Hills" title="Reynolds, Smith &amp; Hills">Reynolds, Smith &amp; Hills</a> as part of a $263 million construction project.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Terminal 4, commonly referred to as the International Terminal, was inaugurated by a <a href="/wiki/Concorde" title="Concorde">Concorde</a> visit in 1983. Since 2005, T4 has been undergoing renovations and a major expansion designed by PGAL/Zyscovich joint venture. The airport announced that Terminal 1, common known as "The New Terminal", underwent $300 million makeover. Construction began in late 2015 and was completed in June 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fort_Lauderdale_%E2%80%93_Hollywood_International_Airport_terminal_1_check-in.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Fort_Lauderdale_%E2%80%93_Hollywood_International_Airport_terminal_1_check-in.jpg/220px-Fort_Lauderdale_%E2%80%93_Hollywood_International_Airport_terminal_1_check-in.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Fort_Lauderdale_%E2%80%93_Hollywood_International_Airport_terminal_1_check-in.jpg/330px-Fort_Lauderdale_%E2%80%93_Hollywood_International_Airport_terminal_1_check-in.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Fort_Lauderdale_%E2%80%93_Hollywood_International_Airport_terminal_1_check-in.jpg/440px-Fort_Lauderdale_%E2%80%93_Hollywood_International_Airport_terminal_1_check-in.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fort_Lauderdale_%E2%80%93_Hollywood_International_Airport_terminal_1_check-in.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Check-in area at Fort Lauderdale – Hollywood International Airport, Terminal 1</div></div></div>
<h3><span id="Terminal_1:_.22New_Terminal.22_-_Yellow"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_1:_&quot;New_Terminal&quot;_-_Yellow">Terminal 1: "New Terminal" -  Yellow</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Terminal 1: &quot;New Terminal&quot; - Yellow">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl><dd><ul><li>The Yellow Terminal has three concourses (A, B, &amp; C) and 23 gates. Concourse A opened on July 5, 2017 and has 7 gates (A1-A7), Concourse B has 7 gates (B2, B4-B9), and Concourse C has 9 gates (C1-C9). Concourse A mainly serves international travelers.</li>
<li>United Airlines operates a United Club in Concourse C, which opened with the new Terminal in May 2001 as a Continental Airlines Presidents Club.</li>
<li>This terminal is used by Alaska, Allegiant, Bahamasair, Copa, Silver, Southwest, <a href="/wiki/Swoop_(airline)" title="Swoop (airline)">Swoop</a>, United, and WestJet.</li></ul></dd></dl>
<h3><span id="Terminal_2:_.22Delta.22_Terminal_-_Red"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_2:_&quot;Delta&quot;_Terminal_-_Red">Terminal 2: "Delta" Terminal - Red</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Terminal 2: &quot;Delta&quot; Terminal - Red">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl><dd><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fort_Lauderdale_Airport_Terminal_1_hallway.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Fort_Lauderdale_Airport_Terminal_1_hallway.jpg/220px-Fort_Lauderdale_Airport_Terminal_1_hallway.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Fort_Lauderdale_Airport_Terminal_1_hallway.jpg/330px-Fort_Lauderdale_Airport_Terminal_1_hallway.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Fort_Lauderdale_Airport_Terminal_1_hallway.jpg/440px-Fort_Lauderdale_Airport_Terminal_1_hallway.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fort_Lauderdale_Airport_Terminal_1_hallway.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal 1 hallway</div></div></div>
<ul><li>The Red Terminal has one concourse (D) and 9 gates.</li>
<li>Delta Air Lines operates a Sky Club here – one of six clubrooms in the state of Florida.</li>
<li>This terminal is used by Delta and Air Canada.</li>
<li>This terminal is currently undergoing a $100 million modernization, including the expansion of the ticketing area, new ceilings, flooring, paint, the inclusion of more food, drink and retail concessions, lounges, etc.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></dd></dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_3:_Main_Terminal_-_Purple">Terminal 3: Main Terminal - Purple</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Terminal 3: Main Terminal - Purple">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl><dd><ul><li>The Purple Terminal has two concourses (E &amp; F) and 20 gates.</li>
<li>In May 2013, a food court opened in Concourse F. It currently consists of a <a href="/wiki/Pei_Wei_Asian_Diner" title="Pei Wei Asian Diner">Pei Wei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Einstein_Bros._Bagels" title="Einstein Bros. Bagels">Einstein Bros. Bagels</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Steak_%27n_Shake" title="Steak &#39;n Shake">Steak 'n Shake</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>This terminal is used by <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azul" class="mw-disambig" title="Azul">Azul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">JetBlue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Air_Lines" title="Norwegian Air Lines">Norwegian</a>, and some <a href="/wiki/Spirit_Airlines" title="Spirit Airlines">Spirit Airlines</a> flights.</li></ul></dd></dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_4:_International_Terminal_-_Green">Terminal 4: International Terminal - Green</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Terminal 4: International Terminal - Green">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>The Green Terminal has one concourse (G) and 14 gates (G1-G14). Concourse H closed in December 2017 and has since been demolished.</li></ul>
<dl><dd><ul><li>The former Concourse H was reconfigured and redesigned by the architectural firms of PGAL/Zyscovich joint venture. The new three-story facility renamed Concourse G has 14 new gates, 11 of which are international/domestic capable and one arrivals area for bussing operations. New concessions and approximately 50,000 s.f. of administrative offices for the Aviation Department are being designed on the upper levels of the facility.  An expanded Federal Inspection Services facility will also be included in the new Eastern Expansion construction.</li>
<li>This terminal is used by Air Transat, Avianca, British Airways, Caribbean Airlines, Frontier, IBC, SkyBahamas, Spirit, and TAME.</li></ul></dd></dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_Exhibit">Art Exhibit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Art Exhibit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Internationally known artist and sculptor <a href="/wiki/Duane_Hanson" title="Duane Hanson">Duane Hanson</a> created an installation for his work "Vendor with Walkman" at the Departure Level of Terminal 3 at the airport. Hanson, who retired and died in nearby Boca Raton, created a seated middle-aged man wearing a red T-shirt, blue pants, baseball cap and listening to a walkman during a break. The installation accessories give additional clues to the narrative of the artwork: toy airplane, various signs, and announcement for the shop, janitorial supplies.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The artwork has since been moved to Terminal 1 Arrival Level.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_transportation">Ground transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Ground transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Fort Lauderdale–Hollywood International Airport is near the <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lauderdale_Airport_station" title="Fort Lauderdale Airport station">Fort Lauderdale/Hollywood International Airport at Dania Beach train station</a>, served by <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a> <a href="/wiki/Intercity_rail" class="mw-redirect" title="Intercity rail">intercity trains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tri-Rail" title="Tri-Rail">Tri-Rail</a> <a href="/wiki/Commuter_rail" title="Commuter rail">commuter trains</a>. The latter provides a shuttle bus service from the station to three locations at the airport, all on the lower level: the west end of terminal 1, between terminals 2 and 3, and between terminals 3 and 4. The shuttles operate 7 days a week and are free for Tri-Rail customers.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The terminals are accessible by <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_1_in_Florida" title="U.S. Route 1 in Florida">U.S. Route 1</a>. Other major roads that border the airport include <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Road_818" class="mw-redirect" title="Florida State Road 818">Florida State Road 818</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Florida" title="Interstate 95 in Florida">Interstate 95</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Interstate_595_(Florida)" title="Interstate 595 (Florida)">Interstate 595</a>. U.S. Route 1 includes an underpass under Runway 10R/28L.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Real-time_ridesharing" class="mw-redirect" title="Real-time ridesharing">Ride-sharing</a> apps can also be used to and from the airport in designated pickup and drop-off places found between Terminals 1 and 2 and Terminals 3 and 4.
</p><p>The airport also offers airport parking and operates a <a href="/wiki/Consolidated_rental_car_facility" title="Consolidated rental car facility">consolidated rental car facility</a> which can be accessed from Terminal 1 by a short walk and from the other terminals by a free shuttle bus service.
</p><p>FLL is served by <a href="/wiki/Broward_County_Transit" title="Broward County Transit">Broward County Transit</a> bus Route 1 which offers connecting service through the Broward Central Terminal in downtown <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lauderdale" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort Lauderdale">Fort Lauderdale</a>, and also service to <a href="/wiki/Aventura_Mall" title="Aventura Mall">Aventura Mall</a> in <a href="/wiki/Aventura,_Florida" title="Aventura, Florida">Aventura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> in <a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Miami-Dade County">Miami-Dade County</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FedEx_FLL_(29283078487).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/FedEx_FLL_%2829283078487%29.jpg/220px-FedEx_FLL_%2829283078487%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/FedEx_FLL_%2829283078487%29.jpg/330px-FedEx_FLL_%2829283078487%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/FedEx_FLL_%2829283078487%29.jpg/440px-FedEx_FLL_%2829283078487%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2667" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FedEx_FLL_(29283078487).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/FedEx_Express_Flight_910" title="FedEx Express Flight 910">FedEx Express Flight 910</a> experienced a landing gear malfunction in October 2016</div></div></div>
<ul><li>On May 18, 1972, an <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Air_Lines" title="Eastern Air Lines">Eastern Air Lines</a> <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-9-31" class="mw-redirect" title="McDonnell Douglas DC-9-31">McDonnell Douglas DC-9-31</a> had its landing gear collapse and tail section separate during landing. The aircraft then caught fire but all passengers and crew were able to safely evacuate.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On May 26, 1979, an Inter Island Shipping Inc. <b>Howard 350</b> crashed when one engine lost power shortly after takeoff during a forced landing, impacting trees near FLL. Both occupants died. Contaminated fluid was found in the carburetor of the engine.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On July 7, 1983, <a href="/wiki/Air_Florida" title="Air Florida">Air Florida</a> Flight 8 with 47 people on board was flying from <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lauderdale_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort Lauderdale International Airport">Fort Lauderdale International Airport</a> to <a href="/wiki/Tampa_International_Airport" title="Tampa International Airport">Tampa International Airport</a>. One of the passengers handed a note to one of the flight attendants, saying that he had a bomb, and telling them to fly the plane to <a href="/wiki/Havana,_Cuba" class="mw-redirect" title="Havana, Cuba">Havana, Cuba</a>. He revealed a small athletic bag, which he opened, and inside was an apparent explosive device. The airplane was diverted to <a href="/wiki/Havana-Jos%C3%A9_Mart%C3%AD_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Havana-José Martí International Airport">Havana-José Martí International Airport</a>, and the hijacker was taken into custody by Cuban authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On November 19, 2013, an Air Evac International <a href="/wiki/Learjet_35" title="Learjet 35">Learjet 35</a> crashed shortly after take-off from the airport, on its way to <a href="/wiki/Cozumel,_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Cozumel, Mexico">Cozumel, Mexico</a>, after calling <a href="/wiki/Mayday" title="Mayday">mayday</a> and during an attempt to return to the airport, possibly due to engine failure, leaving 4 persons dead.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On October 29, 2015, <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_Airways_Flight_405" title="Dynamic Airways Flight 405">Dynamic Airways Flight 405</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767" title="Boeing 767">Boeing 767-246ER</a> (N251MY) was taxiing to a runway to take off for a flight to <a href="/wiki/Caracas,_Venezuela" class="mw-redirect" title="Caracas, Venezuela">Caracas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>. when its left engine caught fire due to a fuel leak. The crew immediately stopped the airplane and fire crews arrived on the scene. All 101 passengers and crew were evacuated the aircraft, and 17 passengers were transported to a hospital. All runways were shut down and air operations ceased at the airport for three hours.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On October 28, 2016, <a href="/wiki/FedEx_Express_Flight_910" title="FedEx Express Flight 910">FedEx Express Flight 910</a>, a <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-10" title="McDonnell Douglas DC-10">McDonnell Douglas MD-10-10F</a> suffered a landing gear collapse upon landing. The aircraft subsequently caught fire, which destroyed the left wing and engine. The two crew members on board both survived.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On January 6, 2017, a lone gunman <a href="/wiki/2017_Fort_Lauderdale_airport_shooting" class="mw-redirect" title="2017 Fort Lauderdale airport shooting">opened fire</a> inside Terminal 2 with a <a href="/wiki/Semi-automatic_pistol" title="Semi-automatic pistol">semi-automatic handgun</a>, killing 5 people. The shooter surrendered to police and was arrested.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
